‘рдХреНрд╡ рддреНрдпрд╛ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдореН ред рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдпрдордиреБрдХреНрд░рдордгрд┐рдХрд╛ - ‘рдХреНрд╡ рддреНрдпреИрдХрдкрджрд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред тАШ рдЖ рд╡рд╛рдВ рд╕реБрдореНрдиреЗ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢реА рдПрдХрдкрджрд╛ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред ‘рдЖрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирдВ рддреБ ’ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдХреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрд╕реНрддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднреЗ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕реНрдпреБрдХреНрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

63 (504)
As╠Бvins
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except ekapad─Б 11
The first four verses of this hymn are divided more or less equally between the invitation to and journey of the A┼Ыvins to our sacrifice (vss. 1тАУ2) and the sacrifice itself (vss. 3тАУ4). The next two verses (5тАУ6) enter mythological territory: the journey of S┼лry─Б, daughter of the Sun, on the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ chariot along with them. This mytho
logical journey returns us to the actual journey of today (vs. 7) and the hopes we have of these gods when they attend our sacrifice (vs. 8). The final two verses (9тАУ10) are a d─Бnastuti, naming a number of the patrons of the poet, Bharadv─Бja, with the single p─Бda of verse 11 expressing his hope for the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ favor to both himself and his patrons at the place of sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A┼Ыvins The hymn contains many metrical irregularities and a marked tendency towards 10-syl. lines. See Oldenberg for details and disc.

English translation:

тАЬWhere may our praise and oblations find today for a mesenger, those two splendid (A┼Ыvins), the invoked of many, and bring the N─Бsaty─Бs to our presence? Be propitiated (A┼Ыvins) by the adoration of this (your worshipper).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Where today did our reverential praise song, like a messenger, find these two obliging ones, called upon by manyтАФ
(the praise song) that has (previously) turned the N─Бsatyas this way? For you two will be the dearest in his [=poetтАЩs] thought.

Griffith

WHERE hath the hymn with reverence, like an envoy, found both fair Gods to-day, invoked of many-
Hymn that hath brought the two Nasatyas hither? To this man’s thought be ye, both Gods, most friendly.

Geldner

Wo hat die beiden Sch├╢nen, Vielgerufenen heute das dem├╝tige Loblied wie ein Bote angetroffen, das die Nasatya┬┤s oft hierhergebracht hat? Denn ihr sollt in dieses S├дngers Dichtung die Lieblinge sein.

Grassmann

Wo hat die sch├╢nen, vielgerufnen heute das Andachtslied gefunden wie ein Bote, Das nah die beiden treuen hergewandt hat? in dessen Sinn versenket euch am liebsten.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPraised, that you may drink the (sacrificial) Soma, you come promptly upon this my invocation; keep guard around the dwelling against (all) advdrsaries, so that neither one that abides at a distance nor a neighbour may do us harm.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Come fit for this summons of mine, so that, being hymned, you will drink the stalk.
You drive, away from harm, around this circuit, which neither a distant one nor one close by may traverse.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The abl. (or, in principle, gen.) riс╣г├бс╕е is a bit hard to construe. Whenever this form occurs elsewhere (and itтАЩs not rare), it is with a form of either тИЪp─Б or тИЪrakс╣г: тАЬprotect from harm.тАЭ Geldner supplies тАШprotectтАЩ here as well: тАЬ(zum Schutz) gegen Schaden.тАЭ However, in the absence of a lexical тАШprotectтАЩ and in the presence of a verb of motion (y─Бthaс╕е), I take it as an ablative of place from which.

Griffith

Come readily to this mine invocation, lauded with songs, that ye may drink the juices.
Compass this house to keep it from the foeman, that none may force it, either near or distant.

Kommet rechtzeitig auf diese Anrufung von mir, auf da├Я ihr gepriesen den Saft trinket. Ihr macht diese Umfahrt zum Schutz gegen den Schaden, die weder der Fremde noch der Nahestehende ├╝bertreffen kann.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(What is essential) for the copious effusion of the (sacrificial) food has been done for you; the very delicate sacred grass has been strewn; the (priest with) uplifted hands desirous o your presence praises you; the stones express (the Soma), designing it for you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

It has been made for you from the stalk; on the expanse [=ritual ground] has been strewn the ritual grass, offering the easiest
approach.
With hands outstretched, seeking you, I have greeted (you). Approaching you, the stones have anointed you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

There is no expressed subj. to ├бk─Бri and the abl./gen. ├бndhasaс╕е has nothing to depend on. Geldner takes it as a partitive gen. (n. 3a) but simply tr. as an indef. subject (тАЬTrank ist euch bereitetтАЭ), while Renou takes it as belonging to an elliptical construction and suggests supplying either sut├бm or p─Б╠Бntam. I prefer to assume that the subject of ├бk─Бri has been gapped, and ├бndhasaс╕е is an abl. of source.

In this context I take v├бr─лman тАШin/on the expanseтАЩ as referring to the ritual ground on which the barhis has been strewn, rather than simply GeldnerтАЩs тАЬin voller Breite.тАЭ See v├бriman in 11.

vavande is of course ambig. as to person, but given the 1st ps. in 2a and no intermediate 3rd ps. officiant, it is most likely 1st (so also Geldner).

In real-world terms the phrase тАЬthe stones have anointed youтАЭ is, of course, distinctly peculiar. But in the foreshortened universe of RVic discourse, this simply abbreviates the sequence тАЬthe stones pressed out the soma liquid, which was prepared for you to drink, and your drinking of it was as if it were anointing you (and perhaps did, by running down your chins).тАЭ

Griffith

Juice in wide room hath been prepared to feast you: for you the grass is strewn, most soft to tread on.
With lifted hands your servant hath adored you. Yearningfor you the press-stones shed the liquid.

Geldner

Trank ist euch bereitet, in voller Breite ist das Barhis hingelegt, das gern betretene. Mit ausgestreckten H├дnden habe ich euch beneidet, nach euch verlangend. Die ankommenden Pre├Яsteine haben euch geschmeidig gemacht.

Grassmann

Gedient ward euch im weiten Strom des Soma, der Sitz gestreut, der sch├╢n ist zu besteigen, Erhobner Hand verehrte euch der fromme, zu euch hindringend salbten euch die Steine.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAgni is above for you; he is present at (your) sacrifices; the oblation flows diffusive and redolent of gh─л; diligent and zealous is the ministrant priest who is engaged, N─Бsaty─Бs, in your invocation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The fire has stood upright for you at the ceremonies. The gift goes forth, glowing, covered in ghee;
forth the chosen Hotar whose thought is welcomed, who has yoked the N─Бsatyas at his call.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The тАШgiftтАЩ (r─Бt├н-) in b is the ladle containing the ghee. Renou points to passages (III.19.2, IV.6.3) where the ladle is described as r─Бt├нn- тАШpossessing/providing giftsтАЩ.

In d Geldner takes ├бyukta as passive, with the Hotar as subj. and n─Б╠Бsaty─Б as the obj.

of a loc. inf. h├бv─лman: тАЬder eingespant is, die Ns zu laden.тАЭ The pass. interpr. is explicitly rejected by both Oldenberg and Renou, in favor of a rendering like mine. Although GeldnerтАЩs interpr. is appealing in certain ways, there are several things against it: 1) the well-attested mid. root aor. of тИЪyuj is almost always transitive (pass. ├бyukta in V.17.3, I.48.7) – there is after all a distinct passive aor. ├бyoji, ├бyujran to express this function; 2) I know of no instances (nor does Oldenberg) in which loc. h├бv─лman(i) functions as an infin. and takes an object.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬProtectors of many, the daughter of S┼лrya ascended your chariot the defence of hundreds, for refuge sagacious leaders and guides, you have excelled by your devices (all others) at this appearance of the adorable (deities).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Leaders and guides: nar─Б nс╣Ыtyu = guides and dancers; you have excelled: a reference is to the legend of the A┼Ыvins carrying off in their car the daughter of S┼лrya from the other gods, as narrated in Aitareya Br─Бhman.a iv.7

Jamison Brereton

For splendor the Daughter of the Sun mounted your chariot provided with hundredfold help, o you who offer much enjoyment.
You became foremost then in the lineage of those worthy of the sacrifice by your magic powers, o magicians, superior men, dancers.

Griffith

Lords of great wealth! for glory, Surya’s Daughter mounted your car that brings a hundred succours.
Famed for your magic arts were ye, magicians! amid the race of Gods, ye dancing Heroes!

Geldner

Des Surya Tochter hat zur Herrlichkeit euren hunderthelfenden Wagen bestiegen, ihr Vieln├╝tzende. Durch Zauberk├╝nste tatet ihr Zauberkundigen euch dabei hervor unter dem Geschlechte der opferw├╝rdigen G├╢tter, ihr wie T├дnzer geputzte M├дnner.

Grassmann

Zur Pracht bestieg den h├╝lfereichen Wagen der Sonne Tochter, o ihr freudenreichen, Durch Weisheit thut ihr euch hervor, o weise, o pr├дcht’ge M├дnner im Geschlecht der G├╢tter.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou have provided with these beautiful splendours, gratification for the enjoyment of S┼лrya, your horses have descended for feliciy, deserving of praise, the laudation (of the sages) has reached you glorified.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Along with these splendors lovely to see you conveyed the flourishing of S┼лry─Б, for beauty.
The birds flew forth after you, for wonder; (their) choir reached you (so you became) well-praised, o holy ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I assume that тАЬthe flourishing of S┼лry─БтАЭ is simply an elaborate way of saying S┼лry─Б. (Michael Weiss comments simply тАЬCf. Gk. ╬▓╬п╬╖ с╝й╧Б╬▒╬║╬╗╬╡╬п╬╖.тАЭ) Geldner (n. 6b; fld. by Renou) suggests that it is meant to convey that the beauty of S┼лry─Б increases the beauty of the A┼Ыvins but I don’t see this. I take the dat. ┼Ыubh├й in the same way as ┼Ыriy├й (5a and commonly elsewhere, e.g., in the next hymn VI.64.1), v├бpuс╣гe (6c), as vaguely attached datives of purpose/result.

The latter (v├бpuс╣гe) Geldner takes adverbially (тАЬerstaunlichтАЭ), and he construes v─Бm simply as a poss. gen. (тАЬEure Vogel(rosse)тАЭ). I think there is more content here and take ├бnu with v─Бm (тАЬafter/following youтАЭ), separated because v─Бm is taking WackernagelтАЩs position. The beautiful chariot of the beautiful A┼Ыvins carrying the beautiful S┼лry─Б must have been an amazing sight, and the birds in their wonder follow it. As their relative geographical positions indicate (birds after chariot), I think these birds are not, or not only, the Vogelrosse pulling the A┼Ыvins chariot, but also the birds in the world who see the marvel and rise up to accompany it. The songs of the birds in a choir (v─Б╠Бс╣З─л) reach the A┼Ыvins to make them well-praised (s├║с╣гс╣нut─Б). As this indicates, I take s├║с╣гс╣нut─Б as dual (so also Grassmann, Geldner), a proleptic adj.

describing the state of the A┼Ыvins after the birdsongs reach them. However, as Geldner points out (n. 6d), s├║с╣гс╣нut─Б could also be a nom. sg. fem. modifying v─Б╠Бс╣З─л тАШchoir, musicтАЩ, and the adj. is in fact strategically placed between the nom. sg. fem. and the duals. Although a тАЬwell-praised choirтАЭ doesnтАЩt make a lot of sense in this context, Geldner cites VIII.100.11 тАж v─Б╠Бk тАж s├║с╣гс╣нut─Б – though itтАЩs worth pointing out that in that passage the reference is to the goddess Speech, while in our passage, as noted, I take the v─Б╠Бс╣З─л as referring to the тАЬchoirтАЭ of birdsong.

Griffith

Ye Twain, with these your glories fair to look on, brought, to win victory, rich gifts for Surya.
After you flew your birds, marvels of beauty: dear to our hearts! the song, well lauded, reached you.

Mit solchen sehensw├╝rdigen Herrlichkeiten habt ihr eurem Glanz den Zuwachs der Surya zugebracht. Eure Vogelrosse folgen erstaunlich dahin. Es m├╢ge euch, die Sch├╢ngepriesenen des S├дngers Stimme erreichen, ihr …..

Ihr fuhrt mit diesem sehenswerthen Glanze zum Prunksaal hin der Sonnentochter Nahrung; Es flogen eure V├╢gel hin zum Schmucke; Musik drang zu euch, sch├╢n gepries’ne Spender.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay your rapid burden-bearing steeds bring you N─Бsaty─Бs to the (sacrificial) food; your chariot swift as thought has dispensed substantial, desirable, abundant food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let the birds, the horses that convey best, convey you to the pleasurable offering, o N─Бsatyas.
Your chariot swift as thought has been sent surging forth after the many refreshments and the fortifying powers that bring refreshment.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, the chariot journey in this vs. echoes the mythological one in vs. 6 but updated to a wish for the present day.

Geldner divides the 2nd hemistich into two separate clauses, by p─Бda. In this interpr.

the nouns in d are in the nom. pl. and follow the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ chariot that was launched in c (тАЬviele Labsale тАж folgen ihmтАЭ). The published translation takes the two p─Бdas as a single cl., with the nouns in d in the acc. pl. and the chariot following them. Neither of these conjures up an entirely comfortable picture if ├бnu is strictly тАШfollowingтАЩ - either all the good stuff got left behind and has been sent after the chariot, or itтАЩs all zipping along ahead. But my accusative alternative could be taken to mean that the refreshments et al. are already at the ritual ground. This would be supported by ab, esp. b. But it is contra-indicated by VI.62.4 in the immediately preceding A┼Ыvin hymn, where p┼Хkс╣гam and ├нс╣гam are two of the things the A┼Ыvins are bringing.

However, if iс╣г├нdh- is a variant of niс╣гс╣г├нdh- тАШtributeтАЩ (see below), the first of these alternatives is the more likely.

The hapax iс╣г├нdh- is of uncertain formation and meaning, though it obviously falls into the category of desirable things at the ritual. There are (at least) two competing etymologies. One has it as the doublet of niс╣гс╣г├нdh- тАШtributeтАЩ (for lit. see EWA I.198; favored by Renou); the other (see EWA I.200) as a deformation of a putative *iс╣гudh-, like the likewise hapax pс╣Ыkс╣г├║dh- (I.141.4), serving as the base of the denom. iс╣гudhy├б- and cognate to Aves. i┼бud-. The ud(h)- in these forms is explained by Humbach as the zero-grade of the PIE root тИЪ*uedh ╠п тАШleadтАЩ, no longer found in Indo-Aryan as a verbal root. (I suggest an alternative etym. of iс╣гudhy├б- ad I.128.6 and more fully in my forthcoming article тАЬVedic iс╣гudhy├б- and Oldenberg Avestan i┼бud-, i┼б┼лidiia-: The Aim of Praise.тАЭ) Narten (YH 159-63) accepts HumbachтАЩs etym. and further explains our iс╣г├нdh- as altered from *iс╣г├║dh- by folk etymology with тИЪidh тАШkindle, burnтАЩ (162 n. 104) in passages in which the word is connected with Agni, since kindling wood is AgniтАЩs source of strength. This last seems quite weak to me: тАШburnтАЩ contributes no obvious semantics to the noun at least in its only occurrence here – which has nothing to do with Agni – and the iс╣гudhy├б- forms, though not numerous, ought to provide some anchor against such a deformation. For this reason I tentatively follow the first interpr., though only because nothing better seems to be currently on offer. If iс╣г├нdh- is somehow a doublet of niс╣гс╣г├нdh-, which occurs several times with p┼лrv─л╠Бс╕е (III.51.5, VI.44.11) as here, then the reference would be to the tributes that the A┼Ыvins received from the mortal worshippers. I would now alter the tr. to тАЬтАж after the refreshments, fortifying powers, and the many tributes.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬProtectors of many, vast (wealth) is to be distributed by you; give us then nutritious and invariable food. Givers of delight, there are to you, adorers, and fit praise, and libations, which are prepared to acknowledge your liberality.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Nutritious and invariable food: dhenum na iс╣гam pinvatam askr─Бm = give us a cow, food, that does not stray;

Dhenu = pr─лс╣Зayitr─л, gratifying; iс╣гam may be the adjective for eс╣гaс╣З─лyam, give us a desirable cow

Jamison Brereton

Because your giving is much, o you who give much enjoyment, swell our cow and our refreshment (so that they) donтАЩt dry up.
To you belong praises and the good praise-hymn and the juices that have followed your gift, o honeyed ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax ├бsakr─Бm is another proleptic adj. (see 6d). This fem. sg. can apply equally to the two fem. sgs. dhen├║m and iс╣г├бm.

The ├бnu that has not yielded completely satisfactory sense in 6c and 7d here is entirely at home: the various ritual offerings to the A┼Ыvins, both verbal (st├║taс╕е тАж suс╣гс╣нut├нс╕е) and physical (r├бs─Бс╕е, the soma juices), accrue to them following the gift they bestow on the sacrificers.

Griffith

Lords of great wealth, manifold is your bounty: ye filled our cow with food that never faileth.
Lovers of sweetness! yours are praise and singers, and poured libations which have sought your favour.

Geldner

Denn vielfach ist eure Gabe, ihr Vieln├╝tzende. Lasset unsere Kuh, unsere Speise unversieglich schwellen! Euer sind die Lobges├дnge, ihr S├╝├Яlinge, und das Loblied und die Somas├дfte, die eurer Gabe gefolgt sind.

Grassmann

Denn viel, vielgebende, sind eurer Gaben; den Milchtrank lasst, der nie versiegt, uns schwellen; Euch lieblichen sei Lob zu Theil und Lieder und Tr├дnke, die nach eurer Spende strebten.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the two straight-going, light-moving, (mares) of Puraya be mine; may the hundred cows belonging to Sum─лс╕╖ha, may the dressed viands prepared by Peruka be for me; may с╣вaс╣Зс╕Нa bestow upon me ten handsome golden chariots, and obedient, valian, and well-favoured (dependants).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

с╣Ъjre raghv─л = two straight-right-going (vadave, mares);

┼Ъatam = a hundred (gav─Бm, of cows);

Pakva = pakv─Бni (ann─Бni, viands); hiraс╣Зinaс╕е vasm─Бd diс╣гс╣н─лn da┼Ыa = ten golden to us handsome (i.e., rath─Бn, cars); vas┼Ы─Бsaс╕е abi┼Ы─Бca с╣Ыс╣гv─Бn = obedient, valorous, handsome (puruс╣г─Бn, men)

Jamison Brereton

And mine are two silver, swift (mares) of Puraya, a hundred (cows) at (the hands of) Sum─лс╕╖ha, and cooked (foods) at (the hands of) Peruka. ┼Ъ─Бс╣Зс╕Нa has given gold-bedecked (horses) along with their allotted (gear). Ten mated cows are attendant upon the high (horses).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although in the published translation I accept GeldnerтАЩs interpr. of pakv─Б╠Бas тАШcooked (food)тАЩ (so also Grassmann, Hoffmann [231], Klein [DGRV I.97], Scarlatta [587]), in this mass of valuable livestock I now find it unlikely that the poet would memorialize for posterity the gift of a few ready-prepared meals. It is more likely to be a technical term in animal husbandry – perhaps тАШmature(d)тАЩ (тЖР тАШripenedтАЩ), qualifying horses or cattle of a particular age. Although it is neut. pl. and therefore canтАЩt qualify the animals directly, I suggest that parallel to sg. ┼Ыat├бm in the conjoined phrase sum─лс╕╖h├й ┼Ыat├бm peruk├й ca pakv─Б╠Б, we may supply *┼Ыat─Б╠Б(ni) *g├бv─Бm pakv─Б╠БтАЬmature hundreds of cowsтАЭ for тАЬ*hundreds of mature cows.тАЭ A similar constr. seems to be suggested by Grassmann (Nachtr. to ┼Ыat├б-), where he proposes that pakv─Б╠Бbe construed with ┼Ыat├бm as an ex. of his 10) тАЬder Singular neben einem in gleichem Casus stehenden Substantiv des Plurals.тАЭ Although this particular interpr. seems precluded by the ca in the passage, I do think the neut. pakv─Б╠Бqualifies a (gapped) neut. numeral. I would now alter the tr.

to тАЬand (hundreds) of mature (cows) at (the hands of) Peruka.тАЭ Hoffmann (230-31) interprets the two clauses in the 2nd hemistich as modal, with injunc. d─Бt rendered as тАШsoll тАж schenkenтАЩ and the sandhi form abhiс╣г─Б╠Бca interpr.

as an inf. *abhiс╣г─Б╠Бce with the sense тАЬsoll тАж folge.тАЭ This is all in service of his somewhat bizarre insistence that the injunctive aorist doesnтАЩt express immediate past tense (aktuelle Vergangenheit), which is, in his view, the province of the augmented aorist. At least in my view, HoffmannтАЩs restricted and often non-linguistically grounded model of the injunctive has led him to deny the obvious intent of the d─Бnastuti here: the gift generally needs to have been given to be praised! As for the supposed infinitive *abhiс╣г─Б╠Бce (which, it must be admitted, he does not insist on), there are no other such forms, whereas the nom. pl. is attested elsewhere. We must simply accept that it takes verbal rection, here the acc. pl. с╣Ыс╣гv─Б╠Бn; see Scarlatta (587-88).

On sm├бddiс╣гс╣нi- see comm. ad III.45.5.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Purupanth─Б, N─Бsaty─Бs, grant to him who praises you, hundreds and thousands of horses; may he give them, heroes, to Bharadv─Бja; achievers of great deeds, may the r─Бkс╣гasas be slain.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purupanth─Б has given altogether hundreds and thousands of horses for (my) song for you;
to Bharadv─Бja he has given (them) for the song, o hero(es). Demonic powers should be smashed, o you of many wondrous powers.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As in the immediately preceding vs. Hoffmann (230-31) interprets the two forms of d─Бt as modal, тАЬsoll тАж spenden.тАЭ The same objections apply.

The voc. n─Бsaty─Б was omitted in the published translation

The voc. v─лra is stubbornly sg., though the reference must be to the du. A┼Ыvins.

Perhaps, as Michael Weiss suggests, simply a shortened du. voc.

Griffith

Nasatyas! Purupanthas offered hundreds, thousands of steeds to him who sang your praises,
Gave, Heroes! to the singer Bharadvaja. Ye-Wonder-Workers, let the fiends be slaughtered.

Geldner

Purupanthan gab zusammen Hunderte, Tausende von Rossen f├╝r euer Loblied, ihr Nasatya┬┤s. Dem Bharadvaja gab er sie f├╝r das Loblied, ihr Helden. Die Unholde sollen erschlagen sein, ihr Meistertatenreiche.

Grassmann

Eurem S├дnger, o ihr Biederen, gab Purupanthas hunderttausend Rosse; er gab sie jetzt, o M├дnner, dem S├дnger Bharadvadscha; get├╢dtet seien die Gespenster, o thatenreiche.

Elizarenkova
